                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">أَبَوْتُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, [third pers. <foreign lang="ar">أَبَا</foreign>,] (T, S, M, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">أَبَيْتُ</foreign>, [third pers. <foreign lang="ar">أَبَى</foreign>,] (T, M, K,) the latter accord. to Yz, (T,) aor. <foreign lang="ar">آبُو</foreign>, (TK,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">أُبُوَّةٌ</foreign>, (Yz, T, S, Msb,) or this is a simple subst., (M,) <hi rend="ital">I became a father.</hi> (T, * S, * M, K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أَبَوْتُهُ</foreign>, (ISk, T, M, K,) aor. <foreign lang="ar">آبُوهُ</foreign>, (IAar, ISk, T,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">إِبَاوَةٌ</foreign>, (M, K,) <hi rend="ital">I was,</hi> (IAar, ISk, T,) or <hi rend="ital">became,</hi> (M, K,) <hi rend="ital">a father to him.</hi> (IAar, ISk, T, M, K.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [Hence, <hi rend="ital">I fed him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">nourished him;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">reared him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">brought him up.</hi>] You say, <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ يَأْبُو هٰذَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">اليَتِيمَ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">إِبَاوَةٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">Such a one feeds,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">nourishes, this orphan, like as the father does his children.</hi> (Lth, T.) And <foreign lang="ar">مَالَهُ أَبٌ يَأْبُوهُ</foreign> (ISk, T, S) <hi rend="ital">He has not a father to feed him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">nourish him, and to rear him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">bring him up.</hi> (S.)    </entryFree>26:T5dcf,<entryFree id="n116" key="أَبٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">أَبٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> is originally <foreign lang="ar">أَبَوٌ</foreign>, (S, Msb, K,) as is shown by the first of its dual forms and of its pl. forms mentioned below; (S, Msb;) and signifies <hi rend="ital">A father</hi> [in the ordinary sense: and also as meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">an ancestor</hi>]: (M:) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n116-1" target="أَبًا" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, a dial. var., (M, K,) the same in the nom. and accus. and gen. cases, like <foreign lang="ar">قَفًا</foreign>: (M:) and <foreign lang="ar">أَبٌّ</foreign> is a dial. var. of the same, [the second letter being doubled to compensate for the <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> suppressed, as is the case in <foreign lang="ar">أَخٌّ</foreign>, (TA voce <foreign lang="ar">أَخٌ</foreign>)] but is rare. (Msb.) Accord. to the dial. commonly obtaining, when you use it as a prefixed noun, you decline it with the letters <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>, saying, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَاأَبُوهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">This is his father</hi>], (Msb,) and <foreign lang="ar">أَبُوكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">thy father</hi>]; (M;) and <foreign lang="ar">رَأَيْتُ أَبَاهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I saw his father</hi>]; and <foreign lang="ar">مَرَرْتُ بِأَبِيهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I passed by his father</hi>]: (Msb:) but accord. to one dial., you say, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا أَبَاهُ</foreign>, (Msb:) and <foreign lang="ar">أَبَاكَ</foreign>; (M;) and <foreign lang="ar">رَأَيْتُ أَبَاهُ</foreign>; and <foreign lang="ar">مَرَرْتُ بِأَبَاهُ</foreign>: (Msb:) and accord. to one dial., which is the rarest of all, it is defective in every case, like <foreign lang="ar">يَدٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">دَمٌ</foreign>; (Msb;) and [thus] you say, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا أَبُوكَ</foreign> [&amp;c.]. (M.) The dual is <foreign lang="ar">أَبَوَانِ</foreign>, (S, M, Msb,) meaning [<hi rend="ital">two fathers,</hi> and] <hi rend="ital">father and mother;</hi> and some say <foreign lang="ar">أَبَانِ</foreign>: (S, M:) you say, <foreign lang="ar">هُمَاأَبَوَاهُ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">They two are his father and mother;</hi> and in poetry you may say, <foreign lang="ar">هُمَا أَبَاهُ</foreign>; and in like manner, <foreign lang="ar">رَأَيْتُ أَبَيْهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I saw his father and mother</hi>], (T,) and <foreign lang="ar">أَبَيْكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">thy father and mother</hi>]; (S;) but the usual, or chaste, form is <foreign lang="ar">رَأَيْتُ أَبَوَيْهِ</foreign>. (T.) The pl. is <foreign lang="ar">آبَآءٌ</foreign>, (T, S, M, Msb, K,) the best form, (T,) and <foreign lang="ar">أَبُونَ</foreign>, (T, S, M, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">أُبُوٌّ</foreign> (M, K, [in the CK <foreign lang="ar">الاَبْوٌ</foreign> is erroneously put for <foreign lang="ar">الأُبُوٌّ</foreign>,]) and <foreign lang="ar">أُبُوَّةٌ</foreign>, (Lh, T, S, M, K, *) like <foreign lang="ar">عُمُومَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">خُؤُولَةٌ</foreign>: (T, S:) you say, <foreign lang="ar">هٰؤُلَآءِ أَبُوكُمْ</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">آبَاؤُكُمْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">These are your fathers</hi>]; (T;) and hence, in the Kur [ii. 127], accord. to one reading, <foreign lang="ar">وَإِلٰهَ أَبِيكَ إِبرٰهِيمَ وَإِسْمٰعِيلَ وَإِسْحٰقَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And the God of thy fathers, Abraham and Ishmael and Isaac</hi>], meaning the pl. of <foreign lang="ar">أبٌ</foreign>, i. e. <foreign lang="ar">أَبِينَكَ</foreign>, of which the <foreign lang="ar">ن</foreign> is suppressed because the noun is prefixed [to the pronoun]; (S;) and some of the Arabs say, <foreign lang="ar">أَبُوَّتُنَا أَكْرَمُ الآبَآءِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Our fathers are the most generous of fathers</hi>]. (T.) The dim. is   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n116-2" target="أُبَّىٌّ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; originally <foreign lang="ar">أُبَيْوٌ</foreign>, with the final radical letter restored. (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">مَا يَدْرِى لَهُ مِنْ أَبٍ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">مَا أَبٌ</foreign>, mean- <hi rend="ital">ing He knows not who is his father,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">what is his father,</hi> are sayings mentioned by Lh on the authority of Ks. (M.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَبَا لِكَ</foreign>, (T, S, M, K, &amp;c.,) [accord. to the dial. of him who says <foreign lang="ar">أَبًا</foreign> instead of <foreign lang="ar">أَبٌ</foreign>,] as also <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَبَ لَكَ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَبَاكَ</foreign>, (S, K,) [the last, accord. to J, because the <foreign lang="ar">ل</foreign> (meaning the <foreign lang="ar">ل</foreign> in <foreign lang="ar">لك</foreign> in the preceding phrases) is as though it were redundant, but he seems not to have known the dial. var. <foreign lang="ar">أَبًا</foreign>, and I rather think that <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَبَاكَ</foreign>, is for <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَبْقَى ٱللّٰهُ أَبَاكَ</foreign>, or the like,] and <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَبَكَ</foreign>, (Mbr, Sgh, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">لَابَ لَكَ</foreign>, (K,) which is for <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَبَ لَكَ</foreign>, (M,) means Thou art, in my estimation, one deserving of its being said to him, <hi rend="ital">Mayest thou have no father!</hi> it is used in the manner of a proverb, is of frequent occurrence in poetry, (M,) is said to him who has a father and to him who has not a father, and is an imprecation as to the meaning, of necessity, though enunciative as to the letter; (M, K;) and hence the saying of Jereer, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">يَا تَيْمُ تَيْمَ عَدِىٍّ لَا أَبَا لَكُمْ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">O Teym, Teym of 'Ades, may ye have no</hi> 
                  <pb n="11"/> 
                  <hi rend="ital">father!</hi>]; which is the strongest evidence of its being a proverb, and not having a literal meaning; for all of [the tribe of] Teym could not have one father, but all of them were fit objects of imprecation and rough speech: (M:) it is an expression of praise: (S:) [i. e.] it is an imprecation against him to whom it is addressed, not, however, said with the desire of its having effect, but on an occasion of intense love, like <foreign lang="ar">لَا أُمَّ لَكَ</foreign>, &amp;c.: (Har p. 165:) and sometimes in dispraise, like <foreign lang="ar">لَا أُمَّ لَكَ</foreign>: and in wonder, like <foreign lang="ar">لِلّهِ دَرُّكَ</foreign>: (TA:) or, as A Heyth says, on the authority of Aboo-Sa'eed Ed- Dareer, it expresses the utmost degree of reviling; [meaning <hi rend="ital">Thou hast no</hi> known <hi rend="ital">father;</hi>] and <foreign lang="ar">لَا أُمَّ لَكَ</foreign> expresses reviling also, but means Thou hast no free, or ingenuous, mother: (Meyd in Har p. 165: [see <foreign lang="ar">أُمَّ</foreign>:]) sometimes it means <hi rend="ital">Strive,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">exert thyself, in thine affair;</hi> for he who has a father relies upon him in some circumstances of his case: (TA:) accord. to Kh, it means <hi rend="ital">Thou hast none to stand thee in stead of thyself:</hi> (ISh, TA:) Fr says that it is a phrase used by the Arabs [parenthetically, i.e.,] to divide their speech: (TA:) [thus, for instance,] Zufar Ibn-El-Hárith says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">أَرِينِى سِلَاحِى لَا أَبَا لَكَ إِنَّنِى</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">أَرَى الحَرْبَ لَا تَزْدَادُ إِلَّا تَمَادِيَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Show thou me my weapons:</hi> (<hi rend="ital">mayest thou have no father!</hi> or <hi rend="ital">thou hast no father:</hi> &amp;c.:) <hi rend="ital">verily I see the war,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">battle, increases not save in perseverance</hi>]. (TA.) [Aboo-'Alee, as cited in the M, observes that the <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> (meaning the final <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign>) in <foreign lang="ar">أَبَا</foreign>, in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَبَا لَكَ</foreign>, indicates that it is a prefixed noun, and determinate; whereas the <foreign lang="ar">ل</foreign> in <foreign lang="ar">لك</foreign> together with the government exercised upon the noun by <foreign lang="ar">لا</foreign> indicates that it is, on the contrary, indeterminate, and separate from what follows it: but it seems that he was unacquainted with the dial. var. <foreign lang="ar">أَبَّا</foreign>; for <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَبَا لَكَ</foreign> in the dial. of him who uses the form <foreign lang="ar">أَبَّا</foreign> instead of <foreign lang="ar">أَبٌ</foreign> is the same grammatically as <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَبَ لَكَ</foreign> in the dial. of him who uses the form <foreign lang="ar">أَبٌ</foreign>.] Suleymán Ibn-'Abd-El-Melik heard an Arab of the desert, in a year of drought, say, <foreign lang="ar">أَنْزِلْ عَلَيْنَا الغَيْثَ لَا أَبَا لَكَ</foreign>, and Suleymán put the best construction upon it, [as though it meant, <hi rend="ital">Send down upon us rain: Thou hast no father</hi>], and said, I testify that He hath no father nor female companion nor offspring. (TA.) They say also, in paying honour [to a person], <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَبَ لِشَانِئِكَ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَبَ لِشَانِئِكَ</foreign>, (TA,) i. e. <hi rend="ital">May thy hater have no father!</hi> or, accord. to ISk, each is a metonymical expression for <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَبَا لَكَ</foreign>. (S in art. <foreign lang="ar">شنأ</foreign>, q. v.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  One also says, on the occasion of an occurrence that is approved and commended, by way of expressing wonder and praise, <foreign lang="ar">لَلِّهِ أَبُوكَ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">To God, purely, is attributable</hi> [<hi rend="ital">the excellence of</hi>] <hi rend="ital">thy father, seeing that he begat thee a generous son, and produced the like of thee!</hi> (TA;) [or <hi rend="ital">to God be attributed</hi> (<hi rend="ital">the excellence of</hi>) <hi rend="ital">thy father!</hi>] it means that to God [alone] belongs the power to create the like of this man [to whom it relates], from whom has proceeded this wonderful action. (Har p. 44.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">هِىَ بِنْتُ أَبِيهَا</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">She resembles her father in strength of mind,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">spirit, and sharpness of disposition, and in hastening,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">striving to be first, to do things:</hi> said of Hafsah, by 'Áïsheh. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">بِأَبِى</foreign>, (TA,) or <foreign lang="ar">بِأَبِى أَنْتَ</foreign>, (T in art. <foreign lang="ar">بأ</foreign>,) [said to a person,] means [<foreign lang="ar">فُدِيتَ بِأَبِى</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Mayest thou be ransomed with my father!</hi> (see the next sentence but one;) or] <foreign lang="ar">أَفْدِيكَ بِأَبِى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I will ransom thee with my father</hi>]; (T ubi suprà;) or <foreign lang="ar">أَنْتَ مَفْدِىٌّ بِأَبِى</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Thou art,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">shalt be, ransomed with my father</hi>]; or <foreign lang="ar">فَدَيُتُكَ بِأَبِى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I have</hi> in my heart <hi rend="ital">ransomed thee,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">I would ransom thee, with my father</hi>]; the <foreign lang="ar">ب</foreign> being dependent upon a word suppressed, which, accord. to some, is a [pass. participial] noun, and accord. to others, a verb; and this word is suppressed because of the frequent usage of the phrase. (TA.) You say also, <foreign lang="ar">بِأَبِى أَنْتَ وَ أُمِّى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">With my father mayest thou be ransomed, and</hi> with <hi rend="ital">my mother!</hi>]. (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">بِأَبِى مَنْ وَدَدتُّهُ</foreign>, i. e. <foreign lang="ar">فُدِىَ بِأَبِى مَنْ وَدَدتُّهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">May he whom I love be ransomed with my father!</hi>], meaning <hi rend="ital">may he</hi> [<hi rend="ital">my father</hi>] <hi rend="ital">be made a ransom for him</hi> [<hi rend="ital">whom I love</hi>]! (El-Wáhidee on the Deewán of El-Mutanebbee, in De Sacy's Chrest. Arabe, sec. ed. vol. iii. p. 35 of the Arabic text.) Sometimes they change the <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> into <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign>: a poet says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَقَدْ زَعَمُوا أَنِّى جَزِعْتُ عَلَيْهِمَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَهَلْ جَزَعٌ أَنْ قُلْتُ وَا بِأَبَا هُمَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">And they have asserted that I have become impatient on account of them two: but is it</hi> an evidence of <hi rend="ital">impatience that I said, Alas, with my father may they two be ransomed?</hi>]; meaning <foreign lang="ar">وَا بِأَبِى هُمَا</foreign>. (S.) And some of the Arabs used to say, <foreign lang="ar">وَا بِأَبَا أَنْتَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Alas, with my father mayest thou be ransomed!</hi>]: this, says AM, being like <foreign lang="ar">يَا وَيْلَتَا</foreign> for <foreign lang="ar">يَا وَيْلَتِى</foreign>; as also <foreign lang="ar">يَا بَيْبَا</foreign>, with the hemzeh changed into <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>, originally <foreign lang="ar">يَا بِأَبَا</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">يَابِأَبِى</foreign>: and hence what is related, in a trad., of Umm- 'Ateeyeh; that she used not to mention the Prophet without saying, <foreign lang="ar">بِيَبَا</foreign> [for <foreign lang="ar">بِأَبِ هُوَ</foreign>]. (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">بأ</foreign>.) A woman said, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">يَا بِأَبِى أَنْتَ وَ يَا فَوْقَ البِيَبْ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">O</hi> thou to whom I would say, <hi rend="ital">With my father mayest thou be ransomed! and O</hi> thou who art <hi rend="ital">above</hi> him to whom I would address <hi rend="ital">the saying, With my father mayest thou be ransomed!</hi>]; respecting which Fr observes that the two words [<foreign lang="ar">بِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَب</foreign>] are made as one [by prefixing the article] because of their frequent occurrence; (S;) and Aboo-'Alee says that the <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> in <foreign lang="ar">بِيَب</foreign> is substituted for <foreign lang="ar">ء</foreign>, not necessarily; but ISk quotes the words as commencing with <foreign lang="ar">يَا بِيَبَا</foreign>, which is the right reading, in order that this expression may agree with <foreign lang="ar">البِئَبْ</foreign>, which is derived from it: EtTebreezee, however, relates Abu-l-'Alà's reciting the words as ending with <foreign lang="ar">البِئَبْ</foreign>; saying that this is compounded from the phrase <foreign lang="ar">بِأَبِي</foreign>, and that therefore the <foreign lang="ar">ء</foreign> is preserved. (TA.) [See also the first paragraph in art. <foreign lang="ar">بأ</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  You say also, <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَبَتِ</foreign> [meaning <hi rend="ital">O my father</hi>], (S, M, K,) as in <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَبَتِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">افْعَلْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">O my father, do thou</hi> such a thing]; (S;) and <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَبَتَ</foreign>; (S, M, K;) and <foreign lang="ar">يَاأَبَتُ</foreign>; (Z in the Ksh xii. 4;) and <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَبَهْ</foreign> (S, M, K) when you pause after it. (S, M.) The <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>, [here written <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign>,] (Kh, M,) the sign of the fem. gender, (S, Z,) is substituted for the [pronominal] affix <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>, (Kh, S, M, Z,) as in <foreign lang="ar">يَاأُمَّتِ</foreign>; (S;) and is like the <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign> in <foreign lang="ar">عَمَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">خَالَةٌ</foreign>, as is shown by your saying, in pausing, <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَبَهٌ</foreign>, like as you say, <foreign lang="ar">يَا خَالَةٌ</foreign>: (Kh, M:) the annexing of the fem. <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign> to a masc. noun in this case is allowable, like as it is in <foreign lang="ar">حَمَامَةٌ ذَكَرٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">شَاةٌ ذَكَرٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">رَجُلٌ رَبْعَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">غَلَامٌ يَفَعَةٌ</foreign>: its being made a substitute for the affix <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> is allowable because each of these is an augmentative added at the end of a noun: and the kesreh is the same that is in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَبِى</foreign>: (Z ubi suprà:) the <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign> does not fall from <foreign lang="ar">اب</foreign> in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَبَتِ</foreign> when there is no pause after it, though it [sometimes] does from <foreign lang="ar">أُمّ</foreign> in the like phrase in that case, because the former word, being of [only] two letters, is as though it were defective. (S.) <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَبَتَ</foreign> is for <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَبَتَا</foreign>, (Aboo-'Othmán El-Mázinee, S, * M, [the latter expression mentioned also in the K, but not as being the original of the former,]) the <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> [and <foreign lang="ar">ه</foreign>] being suppressed; (the same Aboo- 'Othmán and M;) or for <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَبَتَا</foreign>, the <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> being suppressed, like as the <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> is in <foreign lang="ar">يَا غُلَامِ</foreign>; or it may be after the manner of <foreign lang="ar">يَاأَبِىَ</foreign>. (Z ubi suprà.) <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَبَتُ</foreign> is thus pronounced after the usual manner of a noun ending with the fem. <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>, without regard to the fact that the <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign> is in the former a substitute for the suffix <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>. (Z ubi suprà.) <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَبَهْ</foreign> is said in a case of pause, except in the Kur-án, in which, in this case, you say, <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَبَهْ</foreign>, following the written text; and some of the Arabs pronounce the fem. <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>, in a case of pause, <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign> [in other instances], thus saying, <foreign lang="ar">يَا طَلْحَتُ</foreign>. (S.) <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَبَاهُ</foreign> is also said; (M, K;) though scarcely ever. (M.) A poet uses the expression <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَبَاتَ</foreign>, for <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَبَتَاهْ</foreign>: (S, M:) IB says that this is used only by poetic license, in a case of necessity in verse. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أَبٌ</foreign> is tropically applied to signify <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">A grandfather,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">any ancestor.</hi> (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="9">-b9-</sense>  It is also applied to signify <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">A paternal uncle;</hi> as in the Kur ii. 127, quoted before. (M.)          <sense type="b" n="10">-b10-</sense>  [It is also (like <foreign lang="ar">أُمّ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">اِبْن</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">بِنْت</foreign>) prefixed to nouns of various significations. Most of the compounds thus formed will be found explained in the arts. to which belong the nouns that occupy the second place. The following are among the more common, and are therefore here mentioned, as exs. of different kinds.]          <sense type="b" n="11">-b11-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أَبُو المَرْأَةِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The woman's husband:</hi> (Ibn-Habeeb, M:) it is said in the TS that <foreign lang="ar">الأَبُ</foreign>, in certain of the dials., signifies <hi rend="ital">the husband:</hi> MF deems this meaning strange. (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">أَبُو المَثْوَى</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The master of the dwelling,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">of the place of abode:</hi> (TA:) and <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">the guest.</hi> (K in art. <foreign lang="ar">ثوى</foreign>.) <foreign lang="ar">أَبُو الأَضْيَافِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The very hospitable man.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="12">-b12-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أَبُو الحَارِثِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The lion.</hi> (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">أَبُو جَعْدَةَ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The wolf.</hi> (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">أَبُو</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الحُصَيْنِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The fox.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="13">-b13-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أَبُو جَابِر</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Bread.</hi> (S and K in art. <foreign lang="ar">جبر</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="14">-b14-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أَبُو مَالِكٍ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Extreme old age:</hi> (TA:) and <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">hunger.</hi> (MF in art. <foreign lang="ar">جبر</foreign>.)
